                                  function simpleMask(str, key) {
                                      var result = ''; 
                                      for (var i = 0; i < str.length; ++i)
                                          result += String.fromCharCode(key ^ str.charCodeAt(i));
                                      return result;
                                  }

             <div id="ctl00_description" class="summary">
              An improvement on capturing similarity between strings. The algorithm was developed in C#.
             </div>
             <span id="ctl00_thumbnailUrl" class="date" content="https://www.codeproject.com/script/Articles/Images/article100x80.png"></span> 
            </div> 
            <div id="contentdiv" class="text"> 
             <ul class="download"> 
              <li><a href="/KB/recipes/ImproveStringSimilarity/ImproveStringSimilarity_src.zip">Download source files - 10.8 Kb</a> </li>
             </ul> 
             <h2>Introduction</h2> 
             <p>This article describes a way of capturing the similarity between two strings (or words). String similarity is a confidence score that reflects the relation between the meanings of two strings, which usually consists of multiple words or acronyms. Currently, in this approach I am more concerned on the measurement which reflects the relation between the patterns of the two strings, rather than the meaning of the words.</p> 
             <p>I implemented this algorithm when I was developing a tool to make the matching between XML schemas semi-automatic.</p> 
             <h2>Preparing the ground</h2> 
             <p>In this paper, I have implemented two algorithms:</p> 
             <ul> 
              <li>Levenshtein algorithm[1] </li>
              <li>The Kuhn-Munkres algorithm (also known as the Hungarian method)[2] </li>
             </ul> 
             <p>Without going "deep into theory", if you want to understand these algorithms, please read about them in the algorithm books. Other information about them can be reached at:</p> 
             <ol> 
              <li><a href="http://www.let.rug.nl/~kleiweg/lev/levenshtein.html" target="_blank">Levenshtein</a> </li>
              <li><a href="http://www.math.uwo.ca/~mdawes/courses/344/kuhn-munkres.html" target="_blank">The optimal assignment problem</a> </li>
             </ol> 
             <h2>Problem</h2> 
             <p>The string similarity algorithm was developed to satisfy the following requirements:</p> 
             <ul> 
              <li>A true reflection of lexical similarity - strings with small differences should be recognized as being similar. In particular, a significant sub-string overlap should point to a high level of similarity between the strings. </li>
              <li>A robustness to changes of word order- two strings which contain the same words, but in a different order, should be recognized as being similar. On the other hand, if one string is just a random anagram of the characters contained in the other, then it should (usually) be recognized as dissimilar. </li>
              <li>Language independence - the algorithm should work not only in English, but also in many different languages. </li>
             </ul> 
             <h2>Solution</h2> 
             <p>The similarity is calculated in three steps:</p> 
             <ul> 
              <li>Partition each string into a list of tokens. </li>
              <li>Computing the similarity between tokens by using a string edit-distance algorithm (extension feature: semantic similarity measurement using the WordNet library). </li>
              <li>Computing the similarity between two token lists. </li>
             </ul> 
             <h3>Tokenization</h3> 
             <p>A string is a list of words or abbreviations, it may be composed to follow the Camel or Pascal casing without separator characters. Take an example: ‘fileName’ is being tokenized as “file” and “Name”. This work is done by the <i>tokeniser.cs</i> class.</p> 
             <h2>Compute the similarity between two words</h2> 
             <p>The first method uses an edit-distance string matching algorithm: Levenshtein. The string edit distance is the total cost of transforming one string into another using a set of edit rules, each of which has an associated cost. Levenshtein distance is obtained by finding the cheapest way to transform one string into another. Transformations are the one-step operations of (single-phone) insertion, deletion and substitution. In the simplest version substitutions cost about two units except when the source and target are identical, in which case the cost is zero. Insertions and deletions costs half that of substitutions.</p> 
             <p>This code shows a dynamic implementation of the algorithm:</p>
             <pre lang="cs"><span class="code-keyword">private</span> <span class="code-keyword">int</span> ComputeDistance (<span class="code-keyword">string</span> s, <span class="code-keyword">string</span> t)
{
    <span class="code-keyword">int</span> n=s.Length;
    <span class="code-keyword">int</span> m=t.Length;
    int[,] distance=<span class="code-keyword">new</span> int[n + <span class="code-digit">1</span>, m + <span class="code-digit">1</span>]; <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment"> matrix</span>
    <span class="code-keyword">int</span> cost=<span class="code-digit">0</span>;
    <span class="code-keyword">if</span>(n == <span class="code-digit">0</span>) <span class="code-keyword">return</span> m;
    <span class="code-keyword">if</span>(m == <span class="code-digit">0</span>) <span class="code-keyword">return</span> n;
    <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment">init1</span>
    <span class="code-keyword">for</span>(<span class="code-keyword">int</span> i=<span class="code-digit">0</span>; i <span class="code-keyword">&lt;</span>= n; distance[i, <span class="code-digit">0</span>]=i++);
    <span class="code-keyword">for</span>(<span class="code-keyword">int</span> j=<span class="code-digit">0</span>; j <span class="code-keyword">&lt;</span>= m; distance[0, j]=j++);
    <span class="code-comment">//</span><span class="code-comment">find min distance</span>
    <span class="code-keyword">for</span>(<span class="code-keyword">int</span> i=<span class="code-digit">1</span>; i <span class="code-keyword">&lt;</span>= n; i++)
    {
        <span class="code-keyword">for</span>(<span class="code-keyword">int</span> j=<span class="code-digit">1</span>; j <span class="code-keyword">&lt;</span>= m;j++)
        {
            cost=(t.Substring(j - <span class="code-digit">1</span>, <span class="code-digit">1</span>) == 
                s.Substring(i - <span class="code-digit">1</span>, <span class="code-digit">1</span>) ? <span class="code-digit">0</span> : <span class="code-digit">1</span>);
            distance[i,j]=Min3(distance[i - <span class="code-digit">1</span>, j] + <span class="code-digit">1</span>,
            distance[i, j - <span class="code-digit">1</span>] + <span class="code-digit">1</span>,
            distance[i - <span class="code-digit">1</span>, j - <span class="code-digit">1</span>] + cost);
        }
    }
    <span class="code-keyword">return</span> distance[n, m];
}</pre> 
             <h3>The similarity score</h3> 
             <p>I assume that all relation scores are in the [0, 1] range, which means that if the score gets a maximum value (equal to 1) then the two string are absolutely similar.</p>
             <pre lang="cs"><span class="code-keyword">public</span> <span class="code-keyword">float</span> GetSimilarity(<span class="code-keyword">string</span> string1, <span class="code-keyword">string</span> string2) 
{ 
    <span class="code-keyword">float</span> dis=ComputeDistance(string1, string2);
    <span class="code-keyword">float</span> maxLen=string1.Length;
    <span class="code-keyword">if</span> (maxLen <span class="code-keyword">&lt;</span> string2.Length)
    maxLen = string2.Length;
    <span class="code-keyword">if</span> (maxLen == <span class="code-digit">0</span>.0F)
    <span class="code-keyword">return</span> <span class="code-digit">1</span>.0F;
    <span class="code-keyword">else</span>
    <span class="code-keyword">return</span> <span class="code-digit">1</span>.0F - dis/maxLen; 
}</pre> 
             <h3>Similarity between two token lists</h3> 
             <p>After splitting each string into token lists, we capture the similarity between two strings by computing the similarity of those two token lists, which is reduced to the <i>bipartite graph matching</i> problem. A related classical problem on matching in bipartite graphs is the <i>assignment problem</i>, which is the quest to find the optimal assignment of workers to jobs that maximizes the sum of ratings, given all non-negative ratings <i>Cost[i,j] </i>of each worker <i>i </i>to each job <i>j</i>.</p> 
             <h3>The problem can now be described as follows</h3> 
             <p>Given a graph G(V,E), G can be partitioned into two sets of disjoint nodes X(left) and Y (right) such that every edge connects a node in X with a node in Y, and each edge has a non-negative weight.</p> 
             <ul> 
              <li>X is the set of the first list of tokens. </li>
              <li>Y is the set of the second list of tokens. </li>
             </ul> 
             <p>E is a set of edges connecting between each couple of vertex (X ,Y), the weight of each edge which connects an x<sub>1 </sub>to a y<sub>1 </sub>is computed by the similarity of x<sub>1</sub> token and y<sub>1 </sub>token (using the <code>GetSimilarity</code> function). </p>
             <p></p>
             <pre lang="text">Example: x&lt;SUB&gt;1&lt;/SUB&gt;= "test", y&lt;SUB&gt;1&lt;/SUB&gt;="tet", e(x&lt;SUB&gt;1&lt;/SUB&gt;, y&lt;SUB&gt;1&lt;/SUB&gt;) = 0.75</pre> 
             <p>The task is to find a subset of node-disjoint edges that has the <i>maximum total weight</i>. The similarity of two strings is computed by the number of matched strings.</p> 
             <h3>Initialize the weight of the edges</h3> 
             <p>The results of <code>GetSimilarity</code> function are used to compute the weight of edges.</p>
             <pre lang="cs">w(x,y) = GetSimilarity(token[x], token[y])</pre> 
             <h3>Connecting the edges to maximize the total weight</h3> 
             <p>We use the Hungarian method to solve the maximum total weight of bipartite matching problem. The class used to implement this algorithm is <i>MatchsMaker.cs</i>.</p> 
             <h2>Future improvements</h2> 
             <h3>Computing semantic similarity between words using the WordNet</h3> 
             <p>The above section allows us to get the similarity score between patterns of strings. However, sometimes we need a semantic measurement. This problem leads us to find a semantic similarity. Now, I am experimenting with using WordNet[<sub>1</sub>] to compute the similarity between words inside the English dictionary.</p> 
             <h4>The WordNet</h4> 
             <p>WordNet is a lexical database which is available online and provides a large repository of English lexical items. The WordNet was designed to establish connections between four types of POS (Parts of Speech), noun, verb, adjective, and adverb. The smallest unit in WordNet is synset, which represents a specific meaning of a word. It includes the word, its explanation, and the synonyms of its meaning. The specific meaning of one word under one type of POS is called a sense. Each sense of a word is in a different synset. Synsets are equivalent to senses = structures containing sets of terms with synonymous meanings. Each synset has a gloss that defines the concept it represents. For example the words night, nighttime and dark constitute a single synset that has the following gloss: the time after sunset and before sunrise while it is dark outside. Synsets are connected to one another through explicit semantic relations. Some of these relations (hypernymy, hyponymy for nouns and hypernymy and troponymy for verbs) constitute kind-of and part-of (holonymy and meronymy for nouns) hierarchies. For example, tree is a kind of plant, tree is a hyponym of plant and plant is hypernym of tree. Analogously trunk is a part of tree and we have that trunk is meronym of tree and tree is holonym of trunk. For one word and one type of POS, if there are more than one sense, WordNet organizes them in the order of the most frequently used to the least frequently used.</p> 
             <p>Base on WordNet and its .NET API (that is provided by Troy Simpson); I use synonym and hypernym relations to capture the semantic similarities of tokens. Given a pair of words, once a path that connects the two words is found, I determine their similarity based on two factors: the length of the path and the order of the sense involved in this path.</p> 
             <p>To find a path connection between words we use the breadth-first search to check if they are synonyms. Searching the connection between two words in WordNet is an expensive operation due to the large searching space. We define two restrictions in order to reduce the computational time. The first one is that only synonym relations are considered (hyponym and hypernym will be considered later), since exhausting all the relations is too costly. This restriction is also adopted in some related works. Another restriction is to limit the length of the searching path. If the searcher cannot find a path that has been connected within a limited length, we stop searching and give the result as no path found. Hence, this case should have a substitution, the edit-distance instead.</p> 
             <h4>The similarity score</h4> 
             <p>Due to the synonym consideration, first we use the following formula to calculate the semantic similarity of words score:</p>
             <pre lang="text">WordSim(s,t)=SenWeight(s)*SenWeight(t) / PathLength</pre> 
             <ul> 
              <li>Where <code>s</code> and <code>t</code>: denote the source and target words being compared. </li>
              <li><code>SenseWeight</code>: denotes a weight calculated according to the order of this sense and the count of total senses. </li>
              <li><code>PathLength</code>: denotes the length of the connection path from <code>s</code> to <code>t</code>. </li>
             </ul> 
             <p>(This work is an experiment and is not available in this version, it will soon be released.)</p> 
             <h2>Using the code</h2> 
             <p>Add the similarity project to your workspace. Create a method like the following:</p>
             <pre lang="cs"><span class="code-keyword">public</span> Test()
{
   <span class="code-keyword">string</span> s1=<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">The code project's article"</span>;
   <span class="code-keyword">string</span> s2=<span class="code-string">"</span><span class="code-string">Article of The CodeProject"</span>;
   MatchsMaker match=<span class="code-keyword">new</span> MatchsMaker(s1, s2) ;
   Console.WriteLine(match.Score) ;
}</pre> 
             <p>where <code>s1</code>, <code>s2</code> are two strings for capturing similarity. The <code>match.Score</code> is the similarity score of the two strings. In this example, the score is 0.94.</p>

               <!-- Replace href with your meta and URL information.  --> <a href="https://plus.google.com/share?url=https%3a%2f%2fwww.codeproject.com%2fArticles%2f11157%2fAn-improvement-on-capturing-similarity-between-str" class="popup"> <span class="icon">

                   <g>

                      <td class="subject hover-container"><a class="message-link" name="3942801" parent="0" thread="3942801" href="/Messages/3942801/Heres-an-unsafe-version-to-x-faster-modified.aspx">Heres an unsafe version 2 to 3x faster [modified]</a> <a onclick="return forumControl20902599.Pin(this);" rel="nofollow" href="#" title="Click to pin message"><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/script/Forums/Images/pin.png" border="0" align="top" alt="Pin" width="13px" height="13px"></a>

                 <tr id="F3942801_h1" class="content root selected" style="display:none;"> 
                  <td class="normal" width="100%">
                   <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" width="100%"> 
                    <tbody>
                     <tr valign="top"> 
                      <td class="indent align-right" style="width:20px;"><span class="voteform vertical" ownerid="343884" msgid="3942801" votingtype="GoodOrBad"></span><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/script/Forums/Images/t.gif" height="1px" width="20px" alt=""></td>
                      <td class="text">
                       <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="5px" width="100%"> 
                        <tbody>
                         <tr> 
                          <td>
                           <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" width="100%"> 
                            <tbody>
                             <tr> 
                              <td colspan="2">Thanks for this code it works really nicely, heres an unsafe version of the distance function, it runs about 2-3x faster! <img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/script/Forums/Images/smiley_smile.gif" align="top" alt="Smile | :)"> <br> <br> <pre>        <span class="code-keyword">public</span> <span class="code-keyword">static</span> <span class="code-keyword">unsafe</span> <span class="code-keyword">int</span> StringDistance(<span class="code-keyword">string</span> s1, <span class="code-keyword">string</span> s2)
        {
            <span class="code-keyword">int</span> liLengthS1 = s1.Length;
            <span class="code-keyword">int</span> liLengthS2 = s2.Length;
            <span class="code-keyword">int</span> liColWidth = liLengthS2 + <span class="code-digit">1</span>;
            int[,] distance = <span class="code-keyword">new</span> int[liLengthS1 + <span class="code-digit">1</span>, liColWidth];
&nbsp;
            <span class="code-keyword">int</span> liCost = <span class="code-digit">0</span>;
            <span class="code-keyword">if</span> (liLengthS1 == <span class="code-digit">0</span>) <span class="code-keyword">return</span> liLengthS2;
            <span class="code-keyword">if</span> (liLengthS2 == <span class="code-digit">0</span>) <span class="code-keyword">return</span> liLengthS1;
&nbsp;
            <span class="code-keyword">fixed</span> (char* lpchS1 = s1, lpchS2 = s2)
            <span class="code-keyword">fixed</span> (int* lpiDistance = distance)
            {
                <span class="code-keyword">for</span> (<span class="code-keyword">int</span> liRow = <span class="code-digit">0</span>; liRow <span class="code-keyword">&lt;</span>= liLengthS1; lpiDistance[liRow * liColWidth] = liRow++) ;
                <span class="code-keyword">for</span> (<span class="code-keyword">int</span> liCol = <span class="code-digit">0</span>; liCol <span class="code-keyword">&lt;</span>= liLengthS2; lpiDistance[liCol] = liCol++) ;
&nbsp;
                int* lpiRow = lpiDistance;
                int* lpiRowBefore = lpiDistance;
&nbsp;
                <span class="code-keyword">for</span> (<span class="code-keyword">int</span> liRow = <span class="code-digit">1</span>; liRow <span class="code-keyword">&lt;</span>= liLengthS1; liRow++)
                {
                    lpiRow += liColWidth;
&nbsp;
                    <span class="code-keyword">for</span> (<span class="code-keyword">int</span> liCol = <span class="code-digit">1</span>; liCol <span class="code-keyword">&lt;</span>= liLengthS2; liCol++)
                    {
                        liCost = (lpchS2[liCol - <span class="code-digit">1</span>] == lpchS1[liRow - <span class="code-digit">1</span>] ? <span class="code-digit">0</span> : <span class="code-digit">1</span>);
&nbsp;
                        lpiRow[liCol] =
                            Min3(
                                lpiRowBefore[liCol] + <span class="code-digit">1</span>,
                                lpiRow[liCol - <span class="code-digit">1</span>] + <span class="code-digit">1</span>,
                                lpiRowBefore[liCol - <span class="code-digit">1</span>] + liCost
                            );
                    }
&nbsp;
                    lpiRowBefore += liColWidth;
                }
            }
&nbsp;
            <span class="code-keyword">return</span> distance[liLengthS1, liLengthS2];
        }</pre><br>

                               <div class="parent">
                                <a rel="nofollow" onclick="return forumControl20902599.SwitchMessage(null,2358630);" href="/Messages/2358630/Similarity-between-two-strings.aspx"><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/App_Themes/CodeProject/Img/arrow-up24.png" title="Go to Parent" style="width:16px;height:16px;border:0"></a>
                               </div>If you look at the code you will see that Min3 just returns the minimum of 3 integers:<br> <br> <pre><span class="code-keyword">static</span> <span class="code-keyword">int</span> Min3(<span class="code-keyword">int</span> a, <span class="code-keyword">int</span> b, <span class="code-keyword">int</span> c)
{
    <span class="code-keyword">return</span> Math.Min(Math.Min(a, b), c);
}
</pre><br> <br> should do it nicely.<br></td>

Does anyone have any idea why this could be happening.<br> Thanks<br> -Ty<br> <br> -- modified at 17:17 Tuesday 23rd May, 2006<br> <br> Here are some more details.<br> I have isolated the build options that affect how result of the similarity calculation.                                </div>Strange Solution?<br> I got it working finally.. though I don't quite understand how. <br> I achieved success when i commented out the following lines of code in the GetTotal() method of the BipartiteMatcher class.<br> <br> <pre data-lang-guess="HTML"><span class="code-keyword">&lt;</span><span class="code-leadattribute">br</span><span class="code-attribute"> </span><span class="code-keyword">/</span><span class="code-keyword">&gt;</span>
Trace.WriteLine (_leftTokens[i] + " <span class="code-keyword">&lt;</span><span class="code-leadattribute">-</span><span class="code-keyword">&gt;</span> " + _rightTokens [_outgoing[i]] + " : " + _cost[i, _outgoing[i]]) ;<span class="code-keyword">&lt;</span><span class="code-leadattribute">br</span><span class="code-attribute"> </span><span class="code-keyword">/</span><span class="code-keyword">&gt;</span>
<span class="code-keyword">&lt;</span><span class="code-leadattribute">br</span><span class="code-attribute"> </span><span class="code-keyword">/</span><span class="code-keyword">&gt;</span>
float a=1.0F - System.Math.Max(_leftTokens[i].Length , _rightTokens[_outgoing[i]].Length ) != 0 ? _cost[i, _outgoing[i]]/System.Math.Max(_leftTokens[i].Length , _rightTokens[_outgoing[i]].Length ) : 1;<span class="code-keyword">&lt;</span><span class="code-leadattribute">br</span><span class="code-attribute"> </span><span class="code-keyword">/</span><span class="code-keyword">&gt;</span>
<span class="code-keyword">&lt;</span><span class="code-leadattribute">br</span><span class="code-attribute"> </span><span class="code-keyword">/</span><span class="code-keyword">&gt;</span>
nA += a;	<span class="code-keyword">&lt;</span><span class="code-leadattribute">br</span><span class="code-attribute"> </span><span class="code-keyword">/</span><span class="code-keyword">&gt;</span></pre><br> <br> These lines don's seem to do anything but set the value of a variable that isn't used anywhere... yet somehow it was changing the outcome of the calculation ... but only when compiled in release mode. I am happy to have this working but no less confused as to the cause.<br></td>

                  <td class="subject-line normal " width="100%">
                   <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" width="100%"> 
                    <tbody>
                     <tr> 
                      <td width="38px" class="indent"><a name="xx1485814xx"></a><img height="16px" width="16px" align="top" src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/script/Forums/Images/msg_general.gif" alt="General" title="General"></td>
                      <td class="subject hover-container"><a class="message-link" name="1485814" parent="1479697" thread="1479697" href="/Messages/1485814/Re-Request.aspx">Re: Request</a> <a onclick="return forumControl20902599.Pin(this);" rel="nofollow" href="#" title="Click to pin message"><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/script/Forums/Images/pin.png" border="0" align="top" alt="Pin" width="13px" height="13px"></a>
                       <div class="mobile-only"> 
                        <span class="author">Thanh Dao</span>
                        <span class="date">12-May-06 6:06</span> 
                       </div></td>
                      <td class="icon"><img border="0" src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/App_Themes/CodeProject/Img/icn-member-16.gif" title="member" alt="member" height="16px"></td>
                      <td class="author"><span><a href="/script/Membership/View.aspx?mid=1663098">Thanh Dao</a></span></td>
                      <td class="date"><span>12-May-06 6:06&nbsp;</span></td> 
                     </tr> 
                    </tbody>
                   </table></td> 
                 </tr>
                 <tr id="F1485814_h1" class="content selected" style="display:none;"> 
                  <td class="normal" width="100%">
                   <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" width="100%"> 
                    <tbody>
                     <tr valign="top"> 
                      <td class="indent align-right" style="width:38px;"><span class="voteform vertical" ownerid="1663098" msgid="1485814" votingtype="GoodOrBad"></span><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/script/Forums/Images/t.gif" height="1px" width="38px" alt=""></td>
                      <td class="text">
                       <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="5px" width="100%"> 
                        <tbody>
                         <tr> 
                          <td>
                           <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" width="100%"> 
                            <tbody>
                             <tr> 
                              <td colspan="2">
                               <div class="parent">
                                <a rel="nofollow" onclick="return forumControl20902599.SwitchMessage(null,1479697);" href="/Messages/1479697/Request.aspx"><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/App_Themes/CodeProject/Img/arrow-up24.png" title="Go to Parent" style="width:16px;height:16px;border:0"></a>
                               </div>Hello Paula,<br> <br> I glad that you enjoyed it. As you can read in the article, here are three major steps:<br> - Split up a sentence into word/token. (assuming that in most natural language, a sentence is a sequence of words and delimiters.)<br> - Compute the similarity of two words. (you know what does the similarity mean... )<br> - Compute the similarity of two bag of words.<br> <br> firstly I want to explain little bit about string edit distance problem.<br> Let give a simple game: given two words. and you have three operators to do with a word : replace, insert, delete. If you can find out the least number of steps to transform the first word to the second one, you win. So how will we go about finding the best solution ? Mr, Levenstein has done it. <br> <br> private int ComputeDistance (string s, string t) <br> <br> {<br> <br> int n=s.Length;<br> <br> int m=t.Length;<br> <br> Step 0: Create an NxM matrix called the distance matrix in which each element [i,j] represents the cheapest cost (least number of edit step) of transforming the sequence of first i character (in the s string) to another one sequence of first j character (in the t string). <br> <br> int[,] distance=new int[n + 1, m + 1]; // matrix<br> <br> int cost=0; <br> <br> if(n == 0) return m;<br> <br> if(m == 0) return n; <br> <br> Step 1: Initialize the distance matrix [i, 0] :For each row of the distance matrix, calculate value for the element distance[i, 0] = i. That means the cheapest cost to transform a string of length "i" to a empty string is the total steps of using the delete operation.<br> <br> for(int i=0; i &lt;= n; distance[i, 0]=i++); <br> <br> Step 2: Initialize the distance matrix [0, j] :For each row of the distance matrix, calculate value for the element distance[ 0, j] = j. That means the cheapest cost to transform a string of length "j" to a empty string is the total steps of using the delete operation.<br> <br> for(int j=0; j &lt;= m; distance[0, j]=j++);<br> <br> Step 3: Finding the solution for the problem of size [i,j] . The idea behind this code is bottom-up dynamic programming technique. For each element [i,j] we compute the solution for problem of [i,j] bases on the previous smaller problem. We trarvese the matrix programmatically from smaller to bigger. Repeat step 4 until reach the problem size NxM<br> <br> for(int i=1; i &lt;= n; i++) <br> <br> {<br> <br> for(int j=1; j &lt;= m;j++) <br> <br> {<br> <br> Step 4: Compute the solution for problem of size [i,j] bases on previous smaller problem : [i-1, j], [i,j-1], [i-1, j-1]<br> <br> cost=(t.Substring(j - 1, 1) == s.Substring(i - 1, 1) ? 0 : 1); <br> distance[i,j]=Min3(distance[i - 1, j] + 1, <br> distance[i, j - 1] + 1, <br> distance[i - 1, j - 1] + cost);<br> <br> <br> distance[i,j]=Min3(distance[i - 1, j] + 1, // if we base the problem [i-1, j] we need to insert one character. for example : from ABC to ABCD we need to append "D" to the first string. <br> distance[i, j - 1] + 1, // if we base the problem [i, j - 1] we need to delete one character. for example : from ABCD to ABC we need to delete "D". <br> <br> distance[i - 1, j - 1] + cost);//if we base the problem [i - 1, j - 1] , if the S_characterAt(i-1) = S_characterAt(j-1) we have nothing to do, otherwise if they are different then we need to replace. for example ABCD to ABCE we need to replace "D" to "E".<br> <br> }<br> <br> }<br> <br> return distance[n, m];<br> <br> }<br> <br> The smaller number of distance [n, m] the more similar two strings are.<br> There are several ways to compute the similarity value, may use some co-efficient. In example : Sim = (maxLen - distance[n, m]) / maxlen.<br> <br> The idea of dynamic programming is quite simple. If the perfect solution for the smaller (previous) problem does not affect to the solution for the bigger problem (next) we can compute the prefect solution of the bigger problem based on solution of the previous smaller problems. Let you imagine the representation of problems on a hierarchical tree. A parent node is bigger problem, and a smaller is child node. To compute the solution for the parent node you do not need to look at its descendant just need to care its children.<br> <br> Let me know if I am misunderstand your request and bear with me. I will be back to say about maximize bipartite matching algorithm. (I am currently sinking into research paper <img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/script/Forums/Images/smiley_snore.gif" align="top" alt="Sleepy | :zzz:"> ). <br> <br> <br> <br> Thanh Dao<br></td>

                               <div class="parent">
                                <a rel="nofollow" onclick="return forumControl20902599.SwitchMessage(null,1222436);" href="/Messages/1222436/Hopcroft-Karp.aspx"><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/App_Themes/CodeProject/Img/arrow-up24.png" title="Go to Parent" style="width:16px;height:16px;border:0"></a>
                               </div>hu? what about 'Hopcroft-Karp' ?<br> <br> Anyway I did some carefull reading of your code this time (instead superficial amazed test as before).<br> <br> I already made some 'improvment' I hope you will like.<br> here they are:<br> =================================================<br> public class Levenshtein<br> {<br> public static int Min3(int a, int b, int c)<br> {<br> return a &lt; b ? (a &lt; c ? a : c) : (b &lt; c ? b : c);<br> }<br> /// &lt;summary&gt;<br> /// this distance goes from 0 to 1 + Max(s.Length, t.Length).<br> /// if they have different size they would be different<br> /// <br> public static int GetMaxDistance(string s, string t)<br> {<br> int n = s.Length;<br> int m = t.Length;<br> int[,] distance = new int[n + 1, m + 1]; // matrix<br> int cost = 0;<br> <br> if (n == 0) return m;<br> if (m == 0) return n;<br> <br> for (int i = 0; i &lt;= n; distance[i, 0] = i++) ;<br> for (int j = 0; j &lt;= m; distance[0, j] = j++) ;<br> <br> //find min distance<br> for (int i = 1; i &lt;= n; i++)<br> {<br> for (int j = 1; j &lt;= m; j++)<br> {<br> cost = t[j - 1] == s[i - 1] ? 0 : 1;<br> distance[i, j] = Min3(distance[i - 1, j] + 1,<br> distance[i, j - 1] + 1,<br> distance[i - 1, j - 1] + cost);<br> }<br> }<br> <br> return distance[n, m];<br> }<br> /// &lt;summary&gt;<br> /// this distance goes from 0 to 1 + Min(s.Length, t.Length).<br> /// it will be 1 or 0 if one word is caontained in the other<br> /// <br> public static int GetMinDistance(string s, string t)<br> {<br> int n = s.Length;<br> int m = t.Length;<br> int[,] distance = new int[n + 1, m + 1]; // matrix<br> int cost = 0;<br> <br> if (n == 0) return m;<br> if (m == 0) return n;<br> <br> for (int i = 0; i &lt;= n; distance[i, 0] = i++) ;<br> for (int j = 0; j &lt;= m; distance[0, j] = j++) ;<br> <br> //find min distance<br> for (int i = 1; i &lt;= n; i++)<br> {<br> for (int j = 1; j &lt;= m; j++)<br> {<br> cost = t[j - 1] == s[i - 1] ? 0 : 1;<br> distance[i, j] = Min3(distance[i - 1, j] + 1,<br> distance[i, j - 1] + 1,<br> distance[i - 1, j - 1] + cost);<br> }<br> }<br> <br> if (n &lt; m)<br> {<br> int ret = distance[n, n];<br> for (int i = n + 1; i &lt;= m; i++)<br> {<br> int j = distance[n, i] - (i - n);<br> if (j &lt; ret)<br> ret = j;<br> }<br> return ret;<br> }<br> else<br> {<br> int ret = distance[m, m];<br> for (int i = m + 1; i &lt;= n; i++)<br> {<br> int j = distance[i, m] - (i - m);<br> if (j &lt; ret)<br> ret = j;<br> }<br> return ret;<br> }<br> <br> return distance[n, m];<br> }<br> =================================================<br> public class Tokeniser<br> {<br> static Dictionary&lt;char, char&gt; accent;<br> static Tokeniser()<br> {<br> accent = new Dictionary&lt;char, char&gt;();<br> accent['à'] = 'a';<br> accent['â'] = 'a';<br> accent['ä'] = 'a';<br> accent['á'] = 'a';<br> accent['é'] = 'e';<br> accent['è'] = 'e';<br> accent['ê'] = 'e';<br> accent['ë'] = 'e';<br> accent['ì'] = 'i';<br> accent['î'] = 'i';<br> accent['ï'] = 'i';<br> accent['ò'] = 'o';<br> accent['ô'] = 'o';<br> accent['ö'] = 'o';<br> accent['ù'] = 'u';<br> accent['û'] = 'u';<br> accent['ü'] = 'u';<br> accent['ç'] = 'c';<br> accent['’'] = '\'';<br> accent['ñ'] = 'n';<br> }<br> <br> public static List&lt;string&gt; Tokenize(string str)<br> {<br> Set&lt;char&gt; delimiters = new Set&lt;char&gt;();<br> delimiters.AddRange(new char[] { <br> ' ', '\t', '\r', '\n', ',', <br> '.', ',', ':', ';', '?', '!',<br> '(', ')', '{', '}', '[', ']' });<br> return Tokenize(str, delimiters);<br> }<br> public static List&lt;string&gt; Tokenize(string str, Set&lt;char&gt; delimiters)<br> {<br> List&lt;string&gt; ret = new List&lt;string&gt;();<br> StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder();<br> foreach (char c in str)<br> {<br> char c2 = Simplify(c);<br> <br> if (delimiters.Contains(c2))<br> {<br> if (sb.Length &gt; 0)<br> ret.Add(sb.ToString());<br> sb.Length = 0;<br> }<br> else<br> sb.Append(c2);<br> }<br> if (sb.Length &gt; 0)<br> ret.Add(sb.ToString());<br> <br> return ret;<br> }<br> public static char Simplify(char c)<br> {<br> if (Char.IsSeparator(c))<br> return ' ';<br> c = Char.ToLower(c);<br> if (accent.ContainsKey(c))<br> c = accent[c];<br> return c;<br> }<br> public static string Simplify(string s)<br> {<br> StringBuilder sb = new StringBuilder();<br> foreach (char c in s)<br> sb.Append(Simplify(c));<br> return sb.ToString();<br> }<br> }<br> =================================================<br> <br> <br> -- modified at 7:20 Wednesday 28th September, 2005<br></td>

                              <td colspan="2">it becomes:<br> <br> string beforeConversion = "???????????????????";<br> string afterConversion = "aAaAaAaAeEeEeEeEiIiIiIoOoOoOuUuUuUcC'n";<br> <br> System.Text.StringBuilder sb = new System.Text.StringBuilder(input);<br> <br> for (int i = 0; i &lt; beforeConversion.Length; i++) <br> {<br> char beforeChar = beforeConversion[i];<br> char afterChar = afterConversion[i];<br> <br> sb.Replace(beforeChar, afterChar);<br> }<br> <br> sb.Replace("?, "oe");<br> sb.Replace("?, "ae");<br> <br> <br> I suggest that you handle these characters but their char number, not the char itself. <br> <br> Regards,<br> unruledboy@hotmail.com<br></td>

                      <td class="indent align-right" style="width:38px;"><span class="voteform vertical" ownerid="1663098" msgid="1192891" votingtype="GoodOrBad"></span><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/script/Forums/Images/t.gif" height="1px" width="38px" alt=""></td>

                          <td>
                           <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" width="100%">

                             <tr> 
                              <td colspan="2">
                               <div class="parent">
                                <a rel="nofollow" onclick="return forumControl20902599.SwitchMessage(null,1192699);" href="/Messages/1192699/A-suggestion.aspx"><img src="https://codeproject.global.ssl.fastly.net/App_Themes/CodeProject/Img/arrow-up24.png" title="Go to Parent" style="width:16px;height:16px;border:0"></a>
                               </div>This looks like a regular expression. Personally I was thinking of prefix/suffix matcher that mean if a word is prefix or postfix of another word then say that they're equivalent.<br> Prefix is efficient in case similar acronyms or cognate words. <br> These are syntactic similarity and it may not imply semantic relateness.<br> i.e: "net" and "network" but also the same with "hot" and "hotel". <br> <br> Thanh Dao<br></td>

                               </div><small><b>Unruled Boy wrote:</b></small><br> <i>btw, where is latest source code of WordNet.NET? I did not find it at http://opensource.ebswift.com/WordNet.Net/[^] </i><br> <br> Hello, I'm the one who released WordNet.Net to LGPL (based on the port of Malcom Crowe), great work Thanh!<br> <br> The source is actually linked to the 'Subversion Repository' link on that page. The link is a version controlled source repository, and as you can see if you just go to that web page you would have to be downloading lots of different source files. The way to do it is to get yourself a subversion client and let it do the leg work for you. Once you download the source you can keep it up-to-date with nothing more than a right-click and a menu selection from Windows Explorer.<br> <br> I have made a wiki page on how to use the repository with TortoiseSVN here: <a href="http://www.ebswift.com/Wiki/wikka.php?wakka=WordNetDotNetRepository" rel="nofollow">http://www.ebswift.com/Wiki/wikka.php?wakka=WordNetDotNetRepository</a>[<a href="http://www.ebswift.com/Wiki/wikka.php?wakka=WordNetDotNetRepository" target="_blank" rel="nofollow" title="New Window">^</a>]. <br> <br> ~Troy Simpson<br> <br> http://www.ebswift.com<br></td>

                        function getVotesHistogram(objectId, objectTypeId, containerId, loadingId) {
                            if (!$('#' + containerId).attr('alreadyRequested')){
                                $.ajax({
                                    url: '/script/Ratings/Ajax/Histogram.aspx?obid=' + objectId + '&obtid='+objectTypeId,

                                    }
                                });
                                $('#' + containerId).attr('alreadyRequested', 'true');
                            }
                        }
